\"src/java.base/share/classes/java/security/Provider.java\", \"symbol\": \"putService\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The OpenJDK security provider registration framework is implemented across multiple Java source files that work together to provide a pluggable architecture for cryptographic and security algorithms.\\n\\n## Base Provider Class\\nThe foundation is **java.security.Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/java/security/Provider.java), which serves as the abstract base class for all security providers. It defines the core infrastructure including the **putService()** method (line 1221) that providers use to register algorithmic services, and the inner **Service** class (line 1500) that encapsulates service metadata.\\n\\n## Provider Implementations\\nMultiple concrete provider implementations extend Provider and register their algorithms:\\n\\n1. **sun.security.provider.Sun** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/provider/Sun.java) - Provides core cryptographic algorithms including DSA key/parameter generation, SHA-1 and MD5 digests, SecureRandom, X.509 certificates, PKIX certification path validation, PKCS12/JKS keystores, and Java Policy configuration. It delegates service registration to **SunEntries** helper class.\\n\\n2. **sun.security.rsa.SunRsaSign** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/rsa/SunRsaSign.java) - Provides RSA signatures, RSA key factory, and RSA key pair generation capabilities. Uses **SunRsaSignEntries** helper for service registration.\\n\\n3. **com.sun.crypto.provider.SunJCE** (src/java.base/share/classes/com/sun/crypto/provider/SunJCE.java) - The primary cryptographic provider implementing RSA encryption, DES, Triple DES, AES, Blowfish, ARCFOUR, RC2, PBE (password-based encryption), Diffie-Hellman key agreement, HMAC variants, JCEKS keystore, DHKEM, and ML-KEM. It uses putService() calls with Provider.Service objects to register each algorithm.\\n\\n4. **sun.security.ssl.SunJSSE** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/ssl/SunJSSE.java) - Provides SSL/TLS infrastructure including KeyManagerFactory (SunX509/PKIX implementations), TrustManagerFactory, SSLContext (supporting TLSv1.0 through TLSv1.3 and DTLS variants), and PKCS12 keystore for SSL/TLS communications.\\n\\n5. **sun.security.ec.SunEC** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/ec/SunEC.java) - Implements elliptic curve cryptography including EdDSA signatures (Ed25519/Ed448), ECDSA signatures with various SHA algorithms, EC key factories and key pair generators, and EC parameter specifications.\\n\\n6. **apple.security.AppleProvider** (src/java.base/macosx/classes/apple/security/AppleProvider.java) - Platform-specific provider for macOS integration.\\n\\n## Lazy-Loading Registration Mechanism\\nThe provider registration framework uses lazy-loading to defer instantiation of providers until needed:\\n\\n**sun.security.jca.ProviderConfig** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/ProviderConfig.java) is the central lazy-loading mechanism. It encapsulates provider configuration (name and optional arguments) and implements the **getProvider()** method (line 152) using double-checked locking pattern. The method maintains a mapping of provider names to their concrete classes (lines 168-215), supporting both built-in providers (SUN, SunRsaSign, SunJCE, SunJSSE, SunEC) and dynamically loaded providers through ServiceLoader and reflection-based legacy loading. It initializes the default provider list during class loading (lines 51-56) and maintains special provider configurations for JAR verification.\\n\\n## Public API\\n**java.security.Security** (src/java.base/share/classes/java/security/Security.java) is the public API that applications use to interact with the security provider framework through methods like getProviders() and getProvider(String name).\\n\\nThe architecture enables dynamic provider loading, algorithm pluggability, and separation between provider implementation and provider discovery, making the Java security framework extensible while maintaining backward compatibility.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":277,"cache_read_input_tokens":52033,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":277},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"337ef8f6-85f3-4e0c-98de-fd96b22817d2","uuid":"58b5d2f4-a3f4-43fb-b6a4-b4e4cd4472e1"}

It encapsulates provider configuration (name and optional arguments) and implements the **getProvider()** method (line 152) using double-checked locking pattern.
